    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_105723965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105723965" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369004887p2/2753251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105723965?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who suffer too much real-life excitement and need something to sleep on.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=only-okay">only-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=really-excited-for">really-excited-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=not-even-okay">not-even-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=a-favourite-author">a-favourite-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105723965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7058682306842661348"><i>Disappointment</i>. In the <i>Merriam-Webster’s Dictionary</i> of 2004, the verb “disappoint” is defined as such: to fail to fulfill the expectation or hope of –<br/><br/>I don’t know what exactly went wrong with this book. Maybe Dessen’s becoming lazy – her last three books have left me mourning after her better novels – or maybe she’s just running out of “ever-powerful” things to talk about. Whatever it is that made this book lackluster in the eyes of a dear fan, it’s got to be put to bed here and now. I can’t wat</span>
  <span id="freeText7058682306842661348" style="display:none"><i>Disappointment</i>. In the <i>Merriam-Webster’s Dictionary</i> of 2004, the verb “disappoint” is defined as such: to fail to fulfill the expectation or hope of –<br /><br />I don’t know what exactly went wrong with this book. Maybe Dessen’s becoming lazy – her last three books have left me mourning after her better novels – or maybe she’s just running out of “ever-powerful” things to talk about. Whatever it is that made this book lackluster in the eyes of a dear fan, it’s got to be put to bed here and now. I can’t watch another one of her stories swivel down the drain like this one did, especially knowing that Dessen does contain the talent to write a beautiful book. Let’s hope her series of mediocrity ends here.<br /><br />Mclean plays a game of dancing personas – in each town and school that she transfers into with her father, the restaurant fixer-upper, she changes every little thing about her. She’s been the drama queen, the perky cheerleader, the student-body rep. She left the Real Mclean behind with her betraying mother, and up until when the father and daughter move to Lakeview, she doesn’t ever see Real Mclean breaking free from her memories. Lakeview, though, seems to be a magical town because the people who see the true Mclean, somehow, convince her that maybe it's time to make a home.<br /><br />This book is so freaking long, and so freaking boring, I actually had to convince myself to keep reading. As a fan, I was primarily excited that there was more Dessen to go around, but once I got past the 90 page mark, I was ready for this book to end. One of the main issues with WHTG lies in the pacing – nothing exciting happened in this book, and since there was no tension, it became dull and tedious. The beginning took forever to set into place – actually, I felt like we were <i>always</i> at the beginning – and basically, this book is just Mclean is building her personality back and avoiding phone calls from her mother. I would have been able to deal with this, too, if this characterization had been done well – don’t be fooled into thinking this is a character study, guys, because it certainly is not - but unfortunately, Dessen didn't strike out of the park with this one.<br /><br />I didn’t like Mclean. She was too uninteresting, and she just didn’t bring anything to the table. In the YA world where there is such a variety of character-driven novels, leads <i>have</i> to bring something to the table in order to be memorable. Like the protagonist from Along for the Ride, Mclean’s name is forgettable, as well are the other characters. Dave, the love interest in WHTG, had the potential to be another one of Dessen’s fantastic characters, and yet, he too was just average, and not in the good way, either. The only one who caught my eye was Deb because of her interesting experiences and pasts, and if Dessen had stopped to flesh her out (info-dumping and recalling memories isn’t <i>fleshing</i> out a character) then maybe I wouldn’t have had to sludge through this book.<br /><br />The Truth about Forever was hopeful and motivating and moving. This Lullaby was fun and cynical and real. Just Listen was inspirational and sweet and gorgeous. Someone Like You was tear-wrenching and light-shining and truthful. What Happened to Goodbye was cheesy. It was so, so, so cheesy. <br /><br /><blockquote><i>So much had happened that morning. Yet it was this image, this moment, that I kept going back to hours later, after we’d made it safely to the walkway and gone our separate ways to classes. How it felt to have the world moving beneath me, a hand gripping mine, knowing if I fell, at least I wouldn’t do it alone.</i> Pg 238 of What Happened to Goodbye</blockquote><br /><br />Really, gag me with a stick. I love Sarah Dessen’s writing – she can place wise advice in strategic places, she can write lyrically and realistically, and she can evoke emotional reactions – but some of the phrases in this book were just too much. The paragraph above isn’t the worst, but it is part of one of the silliest scenes I’ve ever read.<br /><br />Still, I like that Dessen, above everything and all my complaints, was able to discuss the object of having a home. Although I bored of it quickly, I can appreciate the metaphor of Mclean building her town in a set – which basically is meant to symbolize Mclean building a place that she could call home. I thought that Dessen, with her little metaphoric creations sprinkled here and there, was clever and made us look for the main message of her novel, even if the overall product wasn't exactly what I was hoping for.<br /><br />Maybe I’m tired of her mold, I don’t know. Girl has mommy issues, girl has a certain psychological/emotional misunderstanding, girl meets boy, girl creates a <i>quirky!</i> group of friends, girl has big dramatic climax scene (which doesn't work when you don't provide any tension, alas the ending of this book was crap), girl works it out mommy issues and psychological/emotional misunderstandings and girl gets boy – there’s only so many books like this you can take. <br /><br />I'm disappointed, and seriously, Dessen, if another one of your books comes out reading like your last three, I'm afraid you'll be wondering what happened to goodbye.<br /><br />WHAT HAPPENED TO GOODBYE by Sarah Dessen<br />Audience: 12+<br />Rating: 2.5/5<br />Recommend?: If this is going to be your first Dessen read, pick up one of her older novels first. If you’re a fan, though, read it. It has messages underneath all of the hazy plotting and characters, the messages that Dessen so beautifully weaves into her story definitely what you should be looking out for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7058682306842661348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16551856824257204607">This is my twelfth Dessen novel. In the last two years I have read all of her published works and am now waiting for book thirteen. <br/><br/>But back to this one. I really enjoyed this overall. It was understandable why Mclean reacted the way she did to her parents' divorce. I had a hard time liking the mother at all, but she did grow on me a little. <br/><br/>All of the friends that Mclean and her dad make in Lakeview are great. Deb is my favorite.   <span id="freeText16551856824257204607" style="display:none">This is my twelfth Dessen novel. In the last two years I have read all of her published works and am now waiting for book thirteen. <br /><br />But back to this one. I really enjoyed this overall. It was understandable why Mclean reacted the way she did to her parents' divorce. I had a hard time liking the mother at all, but she did grow on me a little. <br /><br />All of the friends that Mclean and her dad make in Lakeview are great. Deb is my favorite. She does some odd things that really remind me of myself. I like Dave for the same reasons; I see myself in his character. Riley, Heather, and Ellis were each fun additions, though I wasn't sure about them at first. Opal was excellent. <br /><br />And then there's Jason. He gets his own paragraph because I would like to see more of him. He was a jerk in <i>The Truth About Forever</i> and <i>Along for the Ride</i>, but he seems to have grown so much here. I would really like a novel where he's our main guy. Please Sarah? Can you give me that? I know you could make it great. <br /><br />This isn't my favorite Dessen novel, but it was really good. It's quite well balanced and it, along with some of her other recent books, shows how much she has grown as a writer. <br /><br />The basketball rivalry was fun to see from a distance. Very North Carolina in tone there. And the restaurant was a nice touch.</span>

It was wherever the people who loved you were, whenever you were together.” </i><br /><br />Another wonderful Sarah Dessen book.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5650455823276894674">Another amazing book by Sarah Dessen. I have no idea how she does it, but I loved and related to the main character so much.<br/>The story follows McLean. After her parents’ divorce she starts living with her father. They travel a lot and doesn’t have time to saddle dawn and have serious friends or relationship. Every time they travel to a different city, McLean changes. Different personalities, different names, never wants something long term.<br/>This was a really sweet and heartwarming about discoverin</span>
  <span id="freeText5650455823276894674" style="display:none">Another amazing book by Sarah Dessen. I have no idea how she does it, but I loved and related to the main character so much.<br />The story follows McLean. After her parents’ divorce she starts living with her father. They travel a lot and doesn’t have time to saddle dawn and have serious friends or relationship. Every time they travel to a different city, McLean changes. Different personalities, different names, never wants something long term.<br />This was a really sweet and heartwarming about discovering yourself, family, trust and change.<br />Sarah Dessen’s books are always so relatable and this one didn’t disappoint. I loved the main character, she was complex, interesting and had great character development. I loved seeing how her relationships with everyone slowly changed when she started to trust them more and grew closer to them. I loved that she didn’t fear change, but also loved how in the end she wanted something permanent. <br />The family dynamics as always were great. Her family is far from perfect. Her parents are divorced, after her mother cheated on her dad. McLean has never forgiven her mother for the end of their marriage. Even though her mother annoyed me sometimes, because she was occasionally a bit childish, I could see her point of view.<br />The romance story with Dave was really cute. I loved that they were also friends. I mean from the start they liked each other, but they had a great friendship and also really knew each other. Also they were so cute!<br />Also the secondary characters were great. They were so much fun. <br />I loved this book!<br /></span>

<div id="review_167446259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167446259" />
    <a title="Joy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/161941-joy"><img alt="Joy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499566705p2/161941.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167446259?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy" href="/user/show/161941-joy">Joy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/161941-joy?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/161941-joy?shelf=21c">21c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/161941-joy?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/161941-joy?shelf=realistic">realistic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer167446259&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167446259" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2351906555410937645">The good thing about Sarah Dessen is that you always know exactly what you're getting when you pick up one of her books. The bad thing is that you always know exactly what you're getting when you pick up one of her books. Dessen may not repeat herself as much as, say, John Green, but her books are definitely all in the same milieu. White teen girl with family issues, cute boy, quirky friends, throw in a blender and hit frappe. Some of the details in this story (the frequent moves, the restaurant</span>
  <span id="freeText2351906555410937645" style="display:none">The good thing about Sarah Dessen is that you always know exactly what you're getting when you pick up one of her books. The bad thing is that you always know exactly what you're getting when you pick up one of her books. Dessen may not repeat herself as much as, say, John Green, but her books are definitely all in the same milieu. White teen girl with family issues, cute boy, quirky friends, throw in a blender and hit frappe. Some of the details in this story (the frequent moves, the restaurant consultant father) worked better than the others (the basketball, the ume.com). The social networking bits seemed particularly contrived--it was virtually forgotten for most of the book, and then remembered just in time for a key scene with McLean and her friends. Um, that's not how teens use Facebook, and let's not pretend that ume.com isn't supposed to be Facebook, just like Defriesne is supposed to be Duke.<br /><br />Overall, a pleasant read, but not one of Dessen's best. I am left wondering what sort of book Dessen might be able to turn out if she stretched herself a little bit and tried to tell a different story next time out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2351906555410937645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_512879744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512879744" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16659000-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587091330p2/16659000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512879744?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/16659000-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142423837" href="/book/show/15812724-what-happened-to-goodbye">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=own-physical">own-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=contemporary-realistic-fiction">contemporary-realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=arcs-and-review-copies">arcs-and-review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=own-multiple-copies">own-multiple-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=swoon">swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16659000-summer?shelf=blog-tour">blog-tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512879744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12338875746619286176"><b>3.5 Stars, Reread May 18, 2017</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495670701i/22844231._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Home wasn’t a set house, or a single town on a map. It was wherever the people who loved you were, whenever you were together. Not a place, but a moment, and then another, building on each other like bricks to create a solid shelter that you take with you for your entire life, wherever you may go.</i>
</blockquote><br/>For the past two years Mclean Sweet and her divorced father have been moving from town to town as he is a restaurant consultant. With each move Mclean sees it as a chan</span>
  <span id="freeText12338875746619286176" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars, Reread May 18, 2017</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495670701i/22844231._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Home wasn’t a set house, or a single town on a map. It was wherever the people who loved you were, whenever you were together. Not a place, but a moment, and then another, building on each other like bricks to create a solid shelter that you take with you for your entire life, wherever you may go.</i>
</blockquote><br>For the past two years Mclean Sweet and her divorced father have been moving from town to town as he is a restaurant consultant. With each move Mclean sees it as a chance to reinvent herself and take up a different persona. As Liz, Eliza, and Beth she’s been many girls from preppy cheerleader to drama diva. But when Mclean and her father make a stop at Lakeview, she’s finds herself as just Mclean. But who is the real Mclean? After being separated from her true identity for so long, Mclean isn’t sure who she really is anymore. With <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> Sarah Dessen weaves yet another story about youth and self discovery.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Outside, the ocean was crashing, waves hitting sand, then pulling back to sea. I thought of everything being washed away, again and again. We make such messes in this life, both accidentally and on purpose. But wiping the surface clean doesn’t really make anything neater. It just masks what is below. It’s only when you really dig down deep, go underground, that you can see who you really are.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Of the books that I’ve read so far by Dessen, I think this one tackles the theme of identity the best</b>. Mainly because I was 100% for the concept behind Mclean’s character.<br><br>As a loyal fan of Dessen’s work, I admit that her books can be formulaic and her female protagonists similiar. But, because of the very fact that Mclean adopts different personas really made her stand out among other Dessen heroines or YA heroines in general to me. And the moment of reveal when her peers and friends discover this secret of hers is shocking and impactful.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>But in the real world, you couldnt really just split a family down the middle, mom on one side, dad the other, with the child equally divided between. It was like when you ripped a piece of paper into two: no matter how you tried, the seams never fit exactly right again. It was what you couldn’t see, those tiniest of pieces, that were lost in the severing, and their absence kept everything from being complete.</i>
</blockquote><br>There are definitely always a lot of conflicting emotions coupled with decisions of separation and divorce for the parties involved, especially if there is the variable of children in the mix, too. As much as it sucks, separation does affect the kids in the family. (But ultimately it’s about thinking whether it’s healthier for all for the two to stay together or be apart.) With this book <b>Sarah Dessen captures how a teenager feels over his/her parents’ separation/divorce perfectly</b>.<br><br>Mclean displays the need of having to side with one parent (in her case her father); personally, I view this is a realistic portrayal of a young teen who is trying to deal with her parents’ divorce. And as someone that was raised by a single dad and has always had a bad relationship with my own mom, I could sympathize and understand Mclean actions even if it seemed impulsive and dramatic. The way she reacts to her mother’s betrayal isn’t at all unreasonable.<br><br>And in the entire plot with the Sweets, I appreciated Dave’s role and involvement in helping Mclean and her parents. Near the end, I really liked that he was able to identify the moment between Mclean and her parents and let them be.<br><br>While on the subject of Mclean’s parents and Dave… This may be an unpopular opinion but <b>I actually interpreted <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> more of a story about family than a romance</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>He thought about this for a second. “True. But if you never really make friends, you probably don’t have anyone to be your 2 a.m. Which would kind of suck.<br>I just looked at him as he stirred his soup, carrots spinning in the liquid. “Your what?”<br>“Two a.m.” He swallowed, then said, “You know. The person you can call at two a.m. and, no matter what, you can count on them. Even if they’re asleep or it’s cold or you need to be bailed out of jail…they’ll come for you. It’s, like, the highest level of friendship.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I mean, there’s still a romance and there are plenty of unconventionally romantic moments. (This time the heroine is moved by receiving a bottle of thyme instead of a bouquet flowers. A bottle of thyme! This is, again, the power of Dessen making mundane moments work.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“So,” he said as we turned onto the main road, the muffler rattling, “I’ve been thinking.”<br>“Yeah?”<br>He nodded. “You really need to go out with me.” <br>I blinked. “I’m sorry?”<br>“You know. You, me. A restaurant or movie. Together.” He glanced over, shifting gears. “Maybe it’s a new concept for you? If so, I’ll be happy to walk you through it.”<br>“You want to take me to a movie?” I asked.<br>“Well, not really,” he said. “What I really want is for you to be my girlfriend. But I thought saying that might scare you off.”</i>
</blockquote><br>But, throughout (re)reading this, <b>I couldn’t decide how I felt about the main couple</b>. I like Mclean and Dave individually but I’m not sure if I liked having them together as a pair. Cute as they were and as much as I felt like they understood each other well for such a short period of time, <b>I wasn’t quite convinced of their chemistry romantically</b>. I actually think I would have preferred Dave and Mclean more as just friends, which was also probably why I subconsciously thought that the romance took more of the backseat compared the family plot now that I think about it. <b>Rarely do I feel this way about Dessen romances but this one didn’t quite build up as smoothly or great as the others by her, in my opinion</b>. Which is why I’ve decided to downrate <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> from 4 stars (what I originally rated this the first time I read it many years ago) to 3.5 stars.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Suddenly, I was just sure he was going to kiss me. He was there, I could feel his breath, the ground solid beneath us. But then something crossed his face, a thought, a hesitation, and he shifted slightly. Not now. Not yet. It was something I’d done so often-weighing what I could afford to risk, right at that moment-that I recognized it instantly. It was like looking in a mirror.</i>
</blockquote><br>However, to my delight, I did catch something (good) about this couple with this reread. Dave and Mclean could be considered as subtle character foils. In the sense that Mclean has always been anyone but herself and she’s reluctant to face who she truly is. While Dave, from since his childhood, has liked the idea of himself changing. He has no trouble accepting who he is and welcomes the person he becomes, including if that means breaking away from his parents’ expectations and boundaries.<br><br>So to conclude, <b>mainly because of the romance, <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> isn’t one of my favorites by Sarah Dessen, but it’s undeniable that the story still possesses a charm</b> that is uniquely Dessen-esque. The cast of characters are relatable and special enough for young teenagers to connect with them easily, and there are a myriad of quotable lines and scenes. This wasn’t like Dessen’s more iconic work such as <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51737.The_Truth_About_Forever" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth About Forever</a>
</i>, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51738.Just_Listen" rel="nofollow noopener">Just Listen</a>
</i>, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22205.This_Lullaby" rel="nofollow noopener">This Lullaby</a>
</i>, and my personal underrated favorite, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5664985-along-for-the-ride" rel="nofollow noopener">Along for the Ride</a>
</i>, but I do think it’s worth reading for Dessen fans or those that have already read the four previously mentioned.<br><br><b>---<br><br>Quotes were taken from a finished review copy.<br><br>---<br><br>Thank you Penguin Random House for the finished review copy of <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i>, as well as inviting and allowing me to participate in the 2017 #ReadADessen blog tour. #PRHPartner<br><br>---<br><br>More reviews at <a href="https://xingsings.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xingsings</a></b><br><br><p><strong><a href="https://xingsings.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a></strong> @xingsings | <strong><a href="https://instagram.com/readxings/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> </strong>@readxings | <strong><a href="https://twitter.com/xingsings" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></strong> @xingsings</p></span>

<div id="review_2052704289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2052704289" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574280006p2/43846663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2052704289?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142423837" href="/book/show/15812724-what-happened-to-goodbye">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2052704289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5705568352380753836"><i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> by Sarah Dessen is a coming of age story that (while being entirely predictable) had a lot of heart. I was getting a lot of <i>Freaks and Geeks</i> vibes from this for some reason even though the stories aren’t really all that similar. But it had that same kind of underdog, uplifting feel that really gets me right in the feels. The only real issue here was that I think the ending was blatantly apparent after reading the first couple chapters. Seriously, I had <u>literally everythi</u></span>
  <span id="freeText5705568352380753836" style="display:none"><i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> by Sarah Dessen is a coming of age story that (while being entirely predictable) had a lot of heart. I was getting a lot of <i>Freaks and Geeks</i> vibes from this for some reason even though the stories aren’t really all that similar. But it had that same kind of underdog, uplifting feel that really gets me right in the feels. The only real issue here was that I think the ending was blatantly apparent after reading the first couple chapters. Seriously, I had <u>literally everything</u> pretty much figured out very early on. But, the story was rather charming so I ended up actually liking this one. <br /><blockquote><b>“It wasn't about being happy or unhappy. I just didn't want to be me anymore.”</b> </blockquote><br />Mclean is our protagonist and she’s on a path to self-discovery. The short version of her past is that her parents had a rather public/messy divorce and she blames her mom for most of it. So she moves in with her Dad (a restaurant consultant) and moves all over the place with him every time he gets a new job. Every time she moves, Mclean decides to just become a different version of herself and have a completely different personality as a way of distancing herself and making it easier to “cut and run” when the time comes to move again. <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> begins with Mclean moving to Lakeview and from here she ends up becoming herself. She confronts a lot of her issues and finally, for the first time in a while, she starts to put down roots. What transpires is Mclean finally getting to know herself amongst her unique group of friends and family. <br /><br />I think the thing that really got me about <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> was the character building. The story itself isn’t all that much as far as compelling plots go. However, I still wanted to know what would happen next because the characters were all so endearing. <b>They were quirky and flawed and I just wanted to knit them all matching sweaters! I don’t know why I want to do that… I don’t even know how to knit. It just feels like something I want all of them to have. </b> I liked that Mclean didn’t move to town and immediately become friends with all the popular kids and then have multiple boys desperately in love with her all while she laments the fact that she’s “plain.” This stayed away from all those overly cliché YA tropes. We got to focus on the <i>Freaks and Geeks<i> type of kids and they are always infinitely more fascinating to me than the cliché YA kids.<br /><blockquote><b>“But anyone can begin. It was the part with all the promise, the potential, the things I loved. More and more, though, I was finding myself wanting to find out what happened in the end...” </b></blockquote><br />This is a book that I normally wouldn’t pick up and I’m glad I decided to anyway. In the end, <i>What Happened to Goodbye</i> was heartwarming. What it lacked in originality it made up for with realistic and loveable characters. I really was quite endeared to these characters living in a rather PG rated teen experience. The only thing holding me back from giving this a 5 star rating is the fact that the story was incredibly predictable. Bottom line: I enjoyed reading this but I wouldn’t necessarily recommend it to other people as a great book.</i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5705568352380753836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BH6C97LN5RXRc6xUUaJY+MoMOE+VnXo2ciWu3xpI08k+WOslCZMsfXZYGDWmV1InHFPfh1sQ9FEpW+hu1wshUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YgdrQy2XRLY1uUildmbtZr0vZ5Bd73I+uK+nXx8lf+dYIQKRlsmN3pKS/MSBk+e5a3CAWJNi/Fnj0eHu0maNfQ==')})
  }
